Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules

The Preferred Option (al-Awla) in Conquered Lands
Hanafi ruling on al-awla in conquered lands with Shafi'i dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two options available to the imam regarding conquered lands, explain when each is preferred (awla), and defend the Hanafi position against the Shafi'i objection using the Sahaba practice and maslaha argument.

Core Idea
The imam may leave conquered land with its inhabitants for perpetual kharaj—a choice validated by Sahaba practice and public interest.

When Muslims conquer a land, the imam faces a choice: distribute the land as ghanima to the fighters or leave it with the original inhabitants in exchange for jizya and kharaj. This passage from al-Hidayah explains which option is preferred (al-awla) depending on the fighters' need, and addresses the Shafi'i objection. The Hanafi school relies on the binding practice of the Sahaba and a strong maslaha argument.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two options and the preference rule
The passage states two options: (1) distribute conquered land as ghanima to fighters, (2) leave land with original inhabitants on condition of jizya. The first is awla when fighters are in need; the second when they are not.
Need (haja) is the criterion that shifts preference.
2
Distinguish movable vs immovable property
For movable property (manqul), granting it as a favor (mann) is impermissible because no sharia precedent exists. For immovable (aqar), ikhtilaf arises with Imam al-Shafi'i.
This distinction is crucial for understanding the scope of the debate.
3
Follow the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that leaving immovable property without distribution nullifies the fighters' ownership rights, and kharaj is not an equivalent countervalue.
The objection is based on qiyas with movable property and the principle of fair compensation.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response and its dalil
The Hanafi response: (a) Sahaba practice (e.g., 'Umar's policy in Iraq) is a binding proof (hujja) overriding qiyas; (b) maslaha: the inhabitants are expert farmers, saving Muslims expense, land remains for future generations, and kharaj accumulates into a large sum over time.
The combination of naqli (Sahaba) and aqli (maslaha) strengthens the position.
5
Apply the condition for leaving land
If the imam chooses to leave the inhabitants on the land, he must also leave sufficient movable property (tools, animals) for them to work, to avoid karaha (dislike).
This ensures the arrangement is practically beneficial.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قِبْلَ الْأَوْلَى هُوَ الْأَوَّلُ عِنْدَ حَاجَةِ الْعَالِمِينَ وَالثَّانِي عِنْدَ عَدَمِ الْحَاجَةِ لِيَكُونَ عُدَةٌ فِي الزَّمَانِ الثَّانِي وَ هَذَا فِي الْعِقَارِاً مَّا فِى الْمَنقُولِ الْمُجَرَّدِ لَا يَجُوزُ الْمَن بِالرَّةِ عَلَيْهِمْ لِأَنَّهُ لَمْ يَرِدْبِهِ الشَّرْعُ فِيهِ وَفِي الْعِقَارِ خِلافُ الشَّافِعِيُّ لِأَنَّ فِى المَن إِبْطَالُ حَقِّ الْعَالِمِينَ اَوْ مِلْكِهِمْ فَلَا يَجُوزُ مِنْ غَيْرِ بَدَلٍ يُعَادِلُهُ وَالْخِرَاجُ غَيْرُ مُعَادِل لِقَتْلِهِ بِخِلَافِ الرِّقَابِ لِأَنَّ لِلْإِمَامِ أَنْ تَبْطُلَ حَقَّهُمْ رَأْسًا بِالْقَتْلِ وَالْحُجَّةُ عَلَيْهِ مَا رَوَيْنَاهُ وَلِأَنَّ فِيْهِ نَظَرَ الأَنَّهُمْ كَالأَكَرَةِ الْعَامِلَةِ لِلْمُسْلِمِينَ الْعَالِمَةِ بِوُجُوهِ الزَّرَاعَةِ وَالْمَوْنُ مُرْتَفِعَةً مَعَ أَنَّهُ يَحْظى بِهِ الَّذِينَ يَأْتُونَ مِنْ بَعْدُ وَالْخِرَاجُ وَإِنْ قَدَّ حَالَا فَقَدْ جَلَّ مَالًا لِدَوَامِهِ وَإِنْ مَنَّ عَلَيْهِمْ بِالرِّقَابِ وَالْأَرَاضِيَ يَدْفَعُ إِلَيْهِمْ مِنَ الْمَنقُولَاتِ بِقَدْرِ مَا يَتَهَيَّا لَهُم الْعَمَلُ لِيَخْرُجَ عَنْ حَدِ الْكَرَاهَةِ ترجمہ اور کہا گیا ہے کہ مذکورہ دوصورتوں میں سے پہلی صورت ( غنیمت کو غازیوں میں تقسیم کر دینا ہی بہتر اور اولی ہے۔ بشرطیکہ غازیوں کو مالی ضرورت زیادہ ہو۔ اور ضرورت نہ ہونے کی صورت میں دوسری صورت اولیٰ ہے ( باشندگان ملک کو اپنی پرانی حالت پر رہنے دینا اور جزیہ دینے کی شرط پر ) تا کہ جب بھی ضرورت آن پڑے اس وقت ان لوگوں کے لئے یہ سامان مہیار ہیں۔ پھر یہ مذکورہ حکم اس صورت میں ہے جبکہ منقولہ جائداد نہ ہو لیکن مال منقولہ کو احسان کے طور پر وہاں کے لوگوں کے پاس واپس کر دینا جائز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ ایسا کرنا شریعت میں منقول نہیں ہے۔ اور غیر منقول یعنی منقول نہ ہونے والی جائداد مثلاً مکانات زمینیں اور باغات وغیرہ کے بارے میں امام شافعی کا اختلاف ہے۔ کیونکہ جن لوگوں پر فتح حاصل کی گئی ہے ان کو مسلمانوں میں تقسیم نہ کر کے ان پر احسان کرتے ہوئے ان کو حسب سابق رکھ کر غازیوں کے حق یا ان کی ملکیت کو باطل کرنا لازم آتا ہے۔ اس طرح یہاں کسی مساوی بدلہ کے بغیر احسان کرنا لازم آتا ہے جو کہ جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور ان سے جو خراج کیا جاتا ہے وہ ان کا پورا بدلہ نہیں ہوتا ہے بخلاف ان لوگوں کے ذات اور رقبہ کے یعنی کافروں کا ملک فتح کیا گیا ہے ان لوگوں کو اپنا غلام بنا کر تقسیم کرناضروری نہیں ہے کیونکہ ان کے بارے میں بھی امام کو اختیار ہوتا ہے کہ اگر ان سب کو قتل بھی کر سکتا ہے۔ پس معلوم ہوا کہ ان غازیوں کا حق ان گرفتار شدہ لوگوں کی ذات اور رقبہ سے متعلق نہیں ہوتا ہے ورنہ امام کو سب کے قتل کر دینے کا بھی اختیار نہ ہوتا۔ اور ہمارا جواب یہ ہے کہ ایسی قیاسی دلیل صحابہ کرام رضی اللہ عنہم کے عمل کے مقابلہ میں باطل ہے کیونکہ فعل صحابہ ایک مسلمہ حجت ہے اور اس دلیل سے بھی کہ ایسا کرنے میں یہ مصلحت ہے کہ اس علاقہ میں جن کفار کو باقی رہنے دیا گیا ہے وہ مسلمانوں کے کا شتکار ہوں گے اور وہ اپنی زمینوں میں زراعت کرنے کے طریقوں سے واقف ہوتے ہیں ۔ اس طرح مسلمانوں کو اس علاقہ میں کھیتی کرنے اور باغات وغیرہ کی دیکھ بھال کرنے کے لئے نہ تو کچھ خرچ کرنا ہوتا ہے اور نہ کوئی فکر ہوتی ہے۔ اس کے علاوہ وہ علاقہ مسلمانوں کی ملکیت میں رہتا ہے جو بعد میں آنے والے مسلمانوں کے لئے ضرورت پڑنے پر ہر طرح کا سامان ثابت ہوتا ہے اور ان سے لیا ہوا خراج اگر چہ فی الحال بظاہر بہت کم ہوتا ہے مگر چونکہ ہمیشہ وصول ہوتا ہے اس لئے بہت زیادہ ہو جاتا ہے اور اگر امام وقت ان کافروں پر احسان کرتے ہوئے ان کی گرد نہیں آزاد کر دے اور ان کو قتل نہ کرے اور وہاں کی زمینوں پر ان کو کاشت کاری کرنے دے تو امام ان لوگوں کے لئے منقولہ جائداد اور سامان میں سے صرف اتنا ہی چھوڑے جن سے وہ اطمینان کے ساتھ کھیتی باڑی کا کام کر سکیں تا کہ کسی طرح کی کراہت بھی نہ پائی جائے۔( کراہت نہ پائی جانے کے جملہ سے اس بات کی طرف اشارہ ہے کہ اگر امام نے ان کی عورتوں اولا د دوسرے اموال سب تقسیم کر دئیے اور ان مردوں کو صرف کاشتکار کے طور پر ان کی زمینوں پر رہنے دیا تو اس میں کراہت ہے کیونکہ وہ مال کے بغیر زمینوں اور کھیتوں سے کسی طرح کا فائدہ نہیں اٹھا سکتے اس لئے کھیتوں اور زمینوں میں کام کرنے کے لائق ان کے پاس مال بھی چھوڑ دینا چاہئے ۔ یہ بات تمر تاشی نے بیان کی ہے
The [preferred] al-awla: the first [option] is when there is need of the fighters, and the second when there is no need, so that it becomes a provision for the later time. This is regarding real estate. As for pure movable property, it is not permissible to grant it as a favor (mann) to them, because the Law has not prescribed it. Regarding real estate, there is disagreement with al-Shafi'i because granting as a favor would nullify the right or ownership of the fighters, so it is not permissible without a countervalue equivalent to it. The kharaj is not equivalent to killing them, unlike the [ownership of] persons, because the Imam has the right to nullify their rights entirely by killing. The proof against him is what we have related, and because in it there is consideration: they are like tenant farmers working for the Muslims, knowledgeable in agricultural methods, and the burden is removed, while at the same time those who come later benefit from it. The kharaj, even if small now, becomes much due to its perpetuity. If he grants favor regarding persons and lands, he should give them from movable goods enough for them to work, so as to avoid any dislike.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi ruling on the preferred option (al-awla) for the imam regarding conquered lands and movable property. The matn states: if the Muslim fighters are in need, distribution is preferred; if not, leaving the land with its original inhabitants on condition of jizya is preferred, so it remains a resource for future Muslims. For movable property (ghanima), granting it back to the conquered people as a favor (mann) is impermissible because no such precedent exists in sharia. For immovable property, Imam al-Shafi'i objects, arguing that leaving the land without distributing it nullifies the fighters' ownership rights, and kharaj is not a sufficient countervalue. The Hanafi response (al-Hujja) is twofold: first, the practice of the Sahaba (e.g., 'Umar in Iraq) is a binding proof (hujja); second, there is a clear maslaha (public interest): the conquered people are expert farmers, their work saves Muslims from trouble and expense, the land remains Muslim property for future generations, and kharaj, though small annually, accumulates into a large sum over time. The passage further notes that if the imam grants favor by leaving their persons and lands, he should also leave sufficient movable property (tools, animals) so they can work the land, avoiding any karaha (dislike). This is according to Tamurtashi.

Key Terms
الأَوْلَى (al-awla): The preferred or better option among permissible choices.
المَنّ (al-mann): Granting conquered people freedom or property without ransom or compensation.
الخَرَاج (al-kharaj): Land tax imposed on conquered non-Muslims who retain their land.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is it permissible to leave conquered lands with the original inhabitants rather than distributing them as ghanima?
A) Because the Sahaba unanimously did so.
B) Because it prevents future wars.
C) Because the inhabitants are expert farmers and the kharaj becomes a perpetual source of revenue.
D) Because the imam has absolute authority without restriction.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the imam has the discretion to leave conquered lands with the original inhabitants on kharaj, supported by Sahaba practice and maslaha, in contrast to the Shafi'i position.

The Imam's Three Options for Prisoners of War
Hanafi ruling on the imam's three options for prisoners of war

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three permissible options the imam has for prisoners of war according to the Hanafi school, and identify which categories are excluded from the dhimma option.

Core Idea
The Hanafi imam may kill, enslave, or release prisoners as dhimmis, but never return them to dar al-harb.

This passage from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar outlines the imam's discretionary authority over captives, a key ruling in the fiqh of jihad. The imam's choice must be guided by public interest (maslaha), and the text also specifies exceptions for Arab polytheists and apostates. Understanding this ruling clarifies the Hanafi approach to balancing security, ethics, and practical benefit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three options
The text lists killing, enslaving, and releasing as dhimmis as the three permissible options for the imam.
2
Examine the proof for killing
The Prophet (peace be upon him) killed prisoners at the conquest of Mecca; this serves as a precedent and a means to eliminate the root of mischief.
Dalil: Sunnah and maqasid.
3
Examine the proof for enslaving
Enslavement repels the prisoners' evil and brings economic benefit to the Muslims.
Dalil: maslaha.
4
Examine the proof for releasing as dhimmis
The caliph 'Umar released prisoners as dhimmis in Iraq, establishing a precedent for this option, provided they pay jizya.
Dalil: practice of the Companions.
5
Note the exceptions and prohibitions
Arab polytheists and apostates cannot be released as dhimmis; they must choose between Islam and death. Also, returning prisoners to enemy territory is absolutely prohibited.
Rulings on exceptions are clear in the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَهُوَ فِي الْأُسارى بِالْخِيَارِ إنْ شَاءَ قَتَلَهُمْ لِأَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ قَدْ قَتَلَ وَلِأَنَّ فِيْهِ حَسْمَ مَادَةِ الْفَسَادِ ترجمہ اور قدوری نے کہا ہے کہ امام کو کا فرقیدیوں کے بارے میں تین باتوں کا اختیار ہوتا ہے کہ اگر چاہے تو ان کو قتل کر دے۔ کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فتح مکہ کے دن قتل کیا تھا۔ اور جیسا کہ بخاری نے اس کی روایت کی ہے۔ اور اس لئے بھی کہ ان کے قتل کر دینے سے فساد کی جڑ کو اکھیڑ دینا ہوتا ہے۔ قیدیوں کو غلام بنانے کا بھی اختیار ہے وَإِنْ شَاءَ اسْتَرَقَهُمْ لِأَنَّ فِيهِ دَفَعَ شَرِهِمْ مَعَ وُفُوْرِ الْمَنْفَعَةِ لِأَهْلِ الْإِسْلَامِ وَإِنْ شَاءَ تَرَكَهُمْ أَحْرَارً ا ذِمَّةٌ لِلْمُسْلِمِينَ الماتِينَا إِلَّا فِى مُشْرِ كى الْعَرَبِ وَالْمُرْتَدِّينَ عَلَى مَا تُبَيِّنْ إِنْ شَاءَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى ترجمہ اور یا اگر امیر چاہے تو ان کو غلام بنالے۔ کیونکہ ایسا کرنے سے ان کی شرارت ختم ہونے کے علاوہ مسلمانوں کو ان سے بہت سے منافع بھی حاصل ہوں گے۔ اور اگر چاہے تو ان کو یوں ہی آزا د ر ہنے دے مگر ان کو ذمی بنا کر ان پر جزیہ لازم کر دے۔ جیسے کہ حضرت عمر رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ نے عراق والوں کے ساتھ کیا تھا۔ البتہ مشرکین عرب اور اسلام سے مرتد ہونے والوں کے ساتھ یہ معاملہ نہ ہو گا کیونکہ ان کیلئے صرف دو ہی باتیں ہیں کہ وہ دوبارہ اسلام قبول کر لیں یا قتل کر دیئے جائیں ۔ انشاء اللہ اس مسئلہ کو ہم تفصیل سے بیان کریں گے۔ سر براہ مملکت کیلئے جنگی قیدیوں کو از روئے احسان دارالحرب کی طرف رہا کرنا جائز نہیں وَلَا يَجُوزُ أَنْ يَّرْدَهُمْ إِلَى دَارِ الْحَرْبِ لِأَنَّ فِيهِ تَغْوِيَتَهُمْ عَلَى الْمُسْلِمِينَ فَإِنْ أَسْلَمُوا لَايَقْتُلُهُمْ لِانْدِفَاعِ الشَّرِيدُونِه وَلَهُ أَنْ يَسْتَرِ فَهُمْ تَوْفِيرًا لِلْمَنْفَعَةِ بَعْدَ الْعِقَادِ سَبَبِ الْمِلْكِ بِخِلَافِ إِسْلَامِهِمْ قَبْلَ الأَخا لأَنَّهُ لَمْ
He said: And regarding prisoners, he has the choice: if he wishes, he may kill them, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) killed, and because it severs the root of mischief. And if he wishes, he may enslave them, because in it is repelling their evil along with abundant benefit for the people of Islam. And if he wishes, he may leave them free as dhimmis for the Muslims, except for Arab polytheists and apostates, as will be explained, God willing. And it is not permissible to send them back to dar al-harb, because that would strengthen them against the Muslims. If they become Muslim, he does not kill them due to the removal of the harm. And he may enslave them to maximize benefit after the cause of ownership has arisen, unlike their Islam before capture, because [the text cuts off].
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi ruling on the imam's discretionary authority over prisoners of war (usara). The matn, quoting al-Quduri, states that the imam has three options: (1) kill them, because the Prophet did so (e.g., at the conquest of Mecca) and killing eliminates the source of mischief; (2) enslave them, as this repels their evil and brings material benefit to Muslims; (3) release them as free dhimmis (non-Muslim subjects) subject to jizya, following the practice of 'Umar in Iraq. However, this third option does not apply to Arab polytheists (mushriki al-Arab) or apostates (murtaddin), for whom only two options exist: accepting Islam or execution. The passage then adds a prohibition: the imam may not return prisoners to dar al-harb (enemy territory) without ransom or release, because that would strengthen the enemy against Muslims. If a prisoner embraces Islam, killing becomes impermissible since the harm is removed. Enslavement is still permitted after capture (since the cause of ownership has arisen), even if the prisoner later converts, unlike conversion before capture (which prevents enslavement). The text cuts off at this point.

Key Terms
الأُسَارى (al-usara): Prisoners of war captured from the enemy.
ذِمَّةٌ (dhimma): A pact of protection granted to non-Muslims living under Islamic rule, requiring payment of jizya.
المُرْتَدُّون (al-murtaddun): Apostates from Islam; they are not eligible for dhimma and must either repent or be executed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which category of prisoners does NOT qualify for being released as dhimmis?
A) Prisoners captured from Byzantine forces.
B) Arab polytheists (mushriki al-Arab).
C) Prisoners who embrace Islam after capture.
D) Prisoners from Persia.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi imam has three permissible courses of action for prisoners of war, but must never return them to enemy territory.

Ruling on Releasing Captives by Ransom or Favor: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on releasing captives with refutation of Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on releasing captives by ransom or favor, explain the Hanafi proofs, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the principle of naskh (abrogation).

Core Idea
Releasing a captive strengthens the enemy — thus the imam cannot release by ransom or favor.

This lesson tackles a key dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools concerning prisoners of war. The Hanafi school holds that the imam has no authority to release a captive by taking ransom (fidyah) or granting freedom as a favor (mann), because doing so would return a combatant to the enemy, strengthening the disbelievers against the Muslims. The Shafi'i school argues that such practices are permitted based on the Quran and the Prophet's sunnah. Understanding the proofs on both sides reveals how the Hanafi school prioritizes the principle of preventing harm to the Muslim community and relies on the concept of abrogation (naskh) to resolve apparent textual conflict.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: the imam cannot release captives to dar al-harb by any means without killing, enslaving, or making them dhimmis.
This applies to all captives, regardless of age or gender, according to Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Identify the opposing school and its evidence
Imam al-Shafi'i cites Quran 47:4 'then either a favor or a ransom' and the Prophet's ransoming of captives at Badr as proof of permissibility.
This is a direct textual evidence that appears to support the opposing view.
3
Follow the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i evidence
The Hanafi school argues that verse 47:4 is abrogated (naskh) by later verses, particularly 9:29 and 9:5, which command fighting polytheists wherever they are found and restrict release only to those who accept Islam.
The Prophet's practice at Badr occurred before the abrogating revelation.
4
Analyze the Hanafi proof from harm prevention
The Hanafi school provides three proofs: (1) Quran 8:12 'strike above necks' implies captivity leads to enslavement or execution, not release; (2) Quran 9:5 commands killing polytheists unless they accept Islam, and ransom does not achieve that; (3) releasing captives strengthens the enemy, causing harm to the Muslims and subjugation of Islam.
These proofs are founded on the principle that Islam must be dominant, not dominated (al-Islam ya'lu wa la yu'la alayh).
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The difference is clear: under Shafi'i, the imam may accept ransom for any captive; under Hanafi, the only options are killing, enslavement, or dhimmi status—no release by ransom or favor.
This has direct implications for military policy and treatment of prisoners.

The Book of Siyar. The cause later becomes effective. 58. Ashraf al-Hidaya, Urdu commentary of Hidaya, volume seven. Translation: And it is not permissible for the imam to grant these captives permission to go to the abode of war. Because doing so would give strength to those disbelievers against the Muslims. Now if they accept Islam, then the imam should not kill them because it becomes possible to avoid their evil and mischief without killing. And the imam also has the right to keep as slaves those captives who have become Muslims, so that many benefits can be obtained from them, because the cause of ownership has been established. That is, they first became captives and slaves, then they became Muslims, so keeping them as slaves is also permissible. In contrast, if those people became Muslims before being captured, then keeping them as slaves is not permissible, because at that time the cause for keeping them as slaves has not arisen. Elaboration: The summary is that the ruler of the state does not have the authority to send any captive back to the abode of war by granting him release as a favor, because by doing so he will fight against the people of Islam and this will strengthen the people of disbelief. Therefore, the Muslim ruler does not have the right to release any disbelieving captive without making him a dhimmi, or without dividing him as spoil of war, or without killing him, or by taking money, or by way of favor. Imam Shafi'i states that it is permissible to release a captive by taking ransom, regardless of what he is like. His evidence is: "Then either a favor afterwards or a ransom" (Muhammad 47:4). Similarly, the Messenger (peace be upon him) released the captives of Badr by taking ransom, and the Messenger's practical act holds at least the degree of permissibility and lawfulness. Therefore, the requirement of the Messenger's act, which is based on permissibility and lawfulness, is that whatever the nature of the captive, it is permissible to release him by taking ransom (money). Imam Muhammad's statement is that concerning an elderly person who lacks the ability to produce offspring, if he is a captive, there is no harm in releasing him by taking money. According to Zahir al-Riwayah (Ziyadat, Jami' al-Kabir, Jami' al-Saghir, Mabsut, Siyar al-Kabir, Siyar al-Saghir), the Hanafi imams hold that releasing a captive by taking money is not permissible. They give three proofs: 1) The command of Allah: "Strike above the necks" (al-Anfal 8:12) – this command pertains to after capture and enslaving, because during battle, striking above the necks, i.e., severing the neck joint, is not possible. 2) "Kill the polytheists wherever you find them" (al-Tawbah 9:5) – abandoning killing is not permissible until the means of accepting Islam is present, which is the purpose of the legislation of killing, and releasing by ransom does not achieve the meaning of the existence of the means. 3) Releasing by taking money or by favor involves assisting and strengthening the people of war in combat. Regarding the elderly person, Imam Muhammad's meaning of assistance is present even in the case of lack of ability to produce offspring, but due to opinion, advice, and increase in numbers, the meaning of strengthening and reinforcement is found in the elderly person. In response to Imam Shafi'i's argument of "Then either a favor afterwards or a ransom", some commentators have stated that the verse "Fight those who do not believe in Allah and the Last Day" (al-Tawbah 9:29) was revealed after Surah Muhammad, so the command "Kill the polytheists" is considered abrogated. If the captive is released as is, it will cause strengthening of the disbelievers and will be harmful to the people of Islam. This harm does not permit releasing the captive by favor or by taking money. Because Islam is dominant, not dominated. By releasing the captive and strengthening the disbelievers, the subjugation of Islam would be realized. Therefore, sending the captive to the abode of war by granting release is not within the authority and right of the Muslim ruler. If a captive accepts Islam during captivity, then killing him will be avoided. Because disbelief in its essence is the source of evil and mischief, a disbeliever is killed due to repelling evil. By accepting Islam, the cause of killing is removed. Thus, with the absence of the cause, the effect (disbelief) is lost. Therefore, upon the captive becoming Muslim, the Muslim ruler is prohibited from killing him. If a disbelieving captive accepts Islam before being captured, he will not be enslaved. Because the cause of ownership was disbelief and capture; upon accepting Islam, the cause of ownership is removed, so enslaving him is not considered correct.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the treatment of prisoners of war. It begins by stating the general Hanafi rule that the imam cannot release captives and send them back to dar al-harb, because this strengthens the enemy. If a captive converts to Islam while in custody, he is not killed (since the reason for killing—repelling evil—is removed), but he can still be enslaved because the cause of ownership (capture) preceded his Islam. However, if he converted before capture, he cannot be enslaved. The text then elaborates that the imam has no right to release a captive by favor, ransom, or any other means without making him a dhimmi, enslaving him, or killing him. Imam Shafi'i's position is presented: releasing captives by ransom is permissible based on Quran 47:4 and the Prophet's practice at Badr. Imam Muhammad adds an exception for elderly captives. The Hanafi response cites three proofs: (1) the command to strike above the necks (8:12) applies after capture, implying captivity is for enslavement, not release; (2) the command to kill polytheists (9:5) is only abandoned upon Islam, and ransom does not provide that alternative; (3) releasing captives strengthens the enemy. The passage then refutes Shafi'i's verse by arguing that it is abrogated by later verses like 9:29 and 9:5, and that releasing captives leads to Islam being subjugated. Finally, it confirms that if a captive converts during captivity, he is not killed; if before capture, he cannot be enslaved.

Key Terms
قیدی (qaydi): A prisoner of war captured by Muslims.
فدیہ (fidyah): Ransom paid for the release of a captive.
منَّہ (manna): Granting freedom as a favor without compensation.
ظاہر الروایات (Zahir al-Riwayah): The six core books of Imam Muhammad: Ziyadat, Jami' al-Kabir, Jami' al-Saghir, Mabsut, Siyar al-Kabir, Siyar al-Saghir.
ناسخ (nasikh): Abrogating verse or ruling that supersedes an earlier one.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what should the imam do with a captive who accepts Islam after being captured?
A) Kill him because he was a disbeliever.
B) Release him immediately as a favor.
C) Not kill him, but he may be kept as a slave.
D) Make him a dhimmi only.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits releasing captives by ransom or favor because it strengthens the enemy and contradicts the principle that Islam should be dominant.

Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules
intermediate
8 min
Exchanging Captives for Muslim Prisoners: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on exchanging captives

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on exchanging captives, explain the rationale behind each position, and identify the mashhur (well-known) position of the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa prohibits all captive exchange; the Sahibayn allow it for Muslim prisoners.

This passage addresses a key intra-Hanafi dispute in the law of jihad: may captives be ransomed or exchanged for Muslim prisoners? Imam Abu Hanifa holds a strict prohibition, while his two main disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, permit exchange when it frees Muslim captives. The text also clarifies the school's well-known position on ransom for money and notes an exception from al-Siyar al-Kabir.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three opinions
List the positions of Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn, and the mashhur of the school regarding exchange for money and for Muslims.
2
Analyze Abu Hanifa's dalil
Explain his reasoning that releasing the captive strengthens the enemy because he will fight again.
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's dalil
Explain their reasoning that freeing a Muslim is better than killing the disbeliever and that the benefit to the Muslim is greater.
4
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
Determine the practical difference: Abu Hanifa prohibits all; Sahibayn allow exchange for Muslims; the mashhur prohibits ransom for money but an exception exists if Muslims have need.
5
Note the additional ruling on converted captives
Understand that if a captive in our hands converts to Islam, he cannot be exchanged because his release would not benefit the Muslim captive and he is trustworthy in his Islam.
This prevents returning a Muslim convert to dar al-harb.

قیدیوں کے بدلے جزیہ لینے کا حکم
وَلَا يُفَادِي بِالْأَسَارَى عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَالَا يُفَادَى بِهِمْ أَسَارَى الْمُسْلِمِينَ وَهُوَ قَوْلُ الشَّافِعِيِّ لِأَنَّ فِيهِ تَخْلِيْصُ الْمُسْلِم وَهُوَ أَوْلَى مِنْ قَتْلِ الْكَافِرِ وَ الْاِنْتِفَاع بِهِ وَلَهُ أَنَّ فِيْهِ مَعُوْنَةَ الْكَفَرَةِ لِأنَّهُ يَعُودُ حَرْباً عَلَيْنَا وَدَفَعُ شَرَحِرَابِهِ خَيْرٌ مِنَ اسْتِلْقَادِ الْأَسِيرِ الْمُسْلِمِ لأَنَّهُ إِذَابَقِيَ فِي أَيْدِيهِمْ كَانَ ابْتِلَاءً فِي حَقَّهِ غَيْرَ مُصَافٍ إِلَيْنَا وَالْإِعَانَةُ بِدَفْعِ أَسِيرِهِمْ إِلَيْهِمُ مُضَابٌ إِلَيْنَا أَمَّا الْمُفَادَاةُ بِمَالٍ يَأْخُذَهُ مِنْهُمْ لَا يَجُوزُ فِى الْمَشْهُورِ مِنَ الْمَذْهَبِ لِمَ بَيَّنَّا وَفِي السَّيْرِ الْكَبِيرِ أَنَّهُ لَا بَأْسَ بِهِ إِذَا كَانَ بِالْمُسْلِمِيْنَ حَاجَةٌ اِسْتِدْلَٓا لَّا بِأَسَارَى بَدْرٍ وَلَو كَانَ أَسْلَمَ الْأَسَارَى فِي أَيْدِينَا لا يُفادى بِمُسْلِم أَسِيرٍ فِي أَيْدِيهِمْ لِأَنَّهُ لَا يُفيدُ إِلَّا إِذَا طَابَتْ نَفْسُهُ بِهِ وَ هُوَ مَامُونَ عَلَى إِسْلَامِهِ
ترجمہ اور ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک کا فرقیدیوں کا فدیہ نہیں لیا جائے گا یعنی یہ بات جائز نہ ہو گی کہ ان سے فدیہ لے کر ان کو چھوڑ دیا جائے اور صاحبین نے فرمایا ہے کہ مسلمان قیدیوں کے بدلے ان کو چھوڑ نا جائز ہے۔ امام شافعی و مالک واحد رحمۃ اللہ علیہم کا بھی یہی قول ہے کیونکہ ایسا کرنے سے ہمارے مسلمان قیدی بھائیوں کو رہائی میسر ہوتی ہے۔ اور یہ بات کا فر کو قتل کر دینے اور اس سے نفع اٹھانے کے مقابلے میں بہت بہتر ہے۔
اور امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ایسا کرنے سے کافروں کو قوت پہنچانی ہوتی ہے کیونکہ یہ قیدی چھوٹ کر ہم سے پھر لڑے گا اور اس کی لڑائی کی برائی اور نقصان کو دور کرنا مسلمان قیدی کو چھڑانے سے بہت بہتر ہے کیونکہ مسلمان قیدی اگر ان کے ہاتھوں میں گرفتار رہا تو
Ruling on taking jizya in exchange for captives. According to Abu Hanifa, there will be no ransom of captives, i.e., it is not permissible to release them by taking ransom. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said that they may be ransomed in exchange for Muslim captives, and that is the statement of al-Shafi'i, because in it there is the freeing of a Muslim, and that is better than killing the disbeliever and benefiting from him. And for him (Abu Hanifa), the evidence is that in it there is assistance to the disbelievers, because he will return as a warrior against us, and repelling his evil is better than rescuing the captive Muslim, because if he remains in their hands, it is a trial for him that does not harm us, while assisting by sending their captive to them is harmful to us. As for ransoming with money taken from them, it is not permissible in the well-known (mashhur) of the school, as we have explained. And in al-Siyar al-Kabir, there is no harm in it if the Muslims have need, using as evidence (the practice with) the captives of Badr. And if the captives in our hands have embraced Islam, they are not to be ransomed with a Muslim captive in their hands, because it only benefits if he (the Muslim captive) is content with it, and he (the converted captive) is trustworthy regarding his Islam. Translation: And according to Abu Hanifa, ransom of disbelieving captives will not be taken, meaning it is not permissible to release them by taking ransom. And the two (Sahibayn) have said that it is permissible to release them in exchange for Muslim captives. Imam Shafi'i and Malik (may Allah have mercy on them) also hold this view, because by doing so our Muslim captive brothers obtain release, and this is much better than killing the disbeliever and taking benefit from him. And Imam Abu Hanifa's evidence is that by doing so, the disbelievers gain strength, because this captive, upon release, will fight us again, and repelling the evil and harm of his fighting is much better than rescuing the Muslim captive, because if the Muslim captive remains in their hands, it is a trial for him that does not harm us.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute and an inter-madhhab dispute regarding exchanging captives. It is titled 'Ruling on taking jizya in exchange for captives' but actually discusses mufadata (exchange) of captives. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that captives should not be ransomed at all, not even in exchange for Muslim captives, because releasing them strengthens the enemy who will fight again. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and Imam al-Shafi'i allow exchanging them for Muslim captives, as this saves a Muslim and is better than killing the disbeliever. The text then notes that according to the well-known (mashhur) position of the Hanafi school, ransoming for money is not permissible, but al-Siyar al-Kabir records an exception if Muslims have need, citing the precedent of Badr captives. Additionally, if a captive in our hands has embraced Islam, he cannot be exchanged for a Muslim captive in their hands, because the exchange only works if the Muslim captive is willing, and the converted captive is trustworthy in his Islam (so he should not be returned to dar al-harb).

Key Terms
مفاداة (mufadat): Exchange of captives, either for money or for other captives.
مشہور (mashhur): The well-known and relied-upon position of the Hanafi school.
استدل لا باسارى بدر (istadalla bi asara Badr): Using the action of the Prophet with the captives of Badr as evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, why is it not permissible to exchange a captive for a Muslim prisoner?
A) Because it is a form of riba.
B) Because the captive, once released, will fight Muslims again and strengthen the enemy.
C) Because Muslim prisoners are not valuable enough.
D) Because the captive might convert to Islam.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, exchanging captives is prohibited by Abu Hanifa but permitted by the Sahibayn when it frees Muslim prisoners; the well-known position prohibits ransom for money, but an exception exists for necessity.

The Ruling on Releasing Captives Without Ransom (Man)
Dispute with Shafi'i on releasing captives without ransom

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on releasing war captives without ransom, identify the Shafi'i counter-argument, and explain the role of naskh in the Hanafi response.

Core Idea
Releasing captives without benefit is invalid because captivity establishes a right of ownership that cannot be waived without compensation.

This lesson examines a classical dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the treatment of war captives. The Hanafi school holds that releasing captives without ransom or benefit is impermissible, while the Shafi'i school allows it based on the Prophet's practice at Badr. We will explore the evidence on both sides and understand how the Hanafi school uses the principle of abrogation (naskh) to resolve the apparent conflict.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and its evidence
Identify the ruling: it is not permissible to release captives without benefit. The primary proof is Quran 9:5, which commands killing polytheists wherever found. Additionally, captivity establishes a right of enslavement that cannot be dropped without benefit or compensation.
The imperative 'faqtulu' indicates obligation (wujub) in Hanafi usul.
2
Identify the opposing view and its proof
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that releasing captives without ransom is permissible. His evidence is the Prophetic action at Badr, where the Prophet (peace be upon him) released some captives without ransom.
This is a sunnah-based argument.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response: abrogation (naskh)
The Hanafi school responds that the Prophetic action is abrogated (naskh) by the later revelation of Quran 9:5. The general command to kill supersedes the earlier specific practice. Understand the principle of naskh: a later revelation overrides an earlier proof when there is a clear conflict.
Naskh is a valid principle in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The practical difference: in the Hanafi school, a commander cannot release captives without receiving some benefit (ransom, exchange, etc.) or must execute or enslave them. In the Shafi'i school, unconditional release is permitted.
Both schools agree on the other options (execution, enslavement, ransom).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَلَا يَجُوزُ الْمَن عَلَيْهِمْ أَى عَلَى الْأَسَارَى خِلَافَا لِلشَّافِعِي فَإِنَّهُ يَقُولُ مَنْ رَسُولُ اللهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ عَلَى بَعْضٍ الأسارى يَوْمَ بَدْروَلَنَا قَوْلُهُ تَعَالَى فَاقْتُلُوا الْمُشْرِكِينَ حَيْثُ وَجَدْتُمُوهُمْ وَلِأَنَّهُ بِالْأَسْرِ وَ الْقَسْرِ يَثْبُتُ حَقٌّ الإِسْترْ فَاقِ فِيهِ فَلَا يَجُوزُ إِسقاطه بِغَيْرِ مَنْفَعَةٍ وَعِوَضٍ وَ مَارَوَاهُ مَنسُوع لِمَا تَلَوْنَا
ترجمہ اور قیدیوں پر احسان کرنا جائز نہیں ہے، بخلاف امام شافعی کے، انکا کہنا یہ ہے کہ آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے غزوہ بدر کے چند قیدیوں پر احسان فرمایا تھا، ہماری دلیل اللہ تعالیٰ کا یہ فرمان ہے (مشرکین جہاں بھی ملیں انکو قتل کر دو ) اور اسلئے بھی ان کو قیدی وفرمانبردار بنا کر غلام بنایا جا سکتا ہے لہذا اس حق کو بلا عوض و بدون منفعت ضائع نہ کیا جائے گا اور امام شافعی کی دلیل ہماری ذکر کردہ آیت کی روشنی میں منسوخ ہو چکی ہے۔
He said: It is not permissible to show favor to them, i.e., to the captives, contrary to al-Shafi'i, for he says that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) showed favor to some of the captives on the day of Badr. And our proof is the saying of the Exalted: 'Kill the polytheists wherever you find them.' And because by captivity and subjugation, the right of enslavement is established in him, so it is not permissible to drop it without benefit and compensation. And what he narrated is abrogated by what we have recited. Translation: And showing favor to captives is not permissible, contrary to Imam Shafi'i, who says that the Prophet (PBUH) showed favor to some captives on the day of Badr. Our proof is the command of Allah: (Kill the polytheists wherever you find them). And also because they can be made captives and slaves; therefore this right should not be wasted without compensation and benefit. And Imam Shafi'i's proof is abrogated in light of the verse we mentioned.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute on the permissibility of releasing war captives without ransom (man). The Hanafi position, based on the generality of the Quranic command to kill polytheists (9:5) and the established right of enslavement through captivity, holds that releasing them without benefit is not allowed. Imam al-Shafi'i argues by citing the Prophet's action at Badr, where he freed some captives. The Hanafi response is that the Prophet's action is abrogated by the verse, and that the right of ownership (through captivity) cannot be waived without compensation. The Hanafi view is preferred as it aligns with the Quranic emphasis on weakening the enemy's power.

Key Terms
المن (al-man): Showing favor to captives by releasing them without ransom or compensation.
الأسر (al-asr): The state of being captured in war; captivity establishes the right of enslavement.
الإسترقاق (al-istirqaq): Enslavement, the right that comes into effect upon capture of disbelievers in jihad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is it not permissible to release war captives without ransom?
A) Because the Prophet never released captives.
B) Because Allah commands killing polytheists wherever found, and capture establishes a right of ownership that cannot be dropped without benefit.
C) Because the imam does not have the authority to release captives.
D) Because all captives must be killed immediately.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits releasing captives without benefit because the right of ownership through captivity is binding, and the Prophetic action at Badr is abrogated by the later general command to kill polytheists.

Hanafi Ruling on Slaughtering Livestock to Prevent Enemy Benefit
Dispute with Shafi'i on slaughtering livestock to prevent enemy use

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on slaughtering livestock when transport is impossible, explain the evidence and the response to the Shafi'i objection, and apply the ruling to a similar scenario.

Core Idea
Slaughtering animals to weaken the enemy is permissible by istihsan, even without intention to eat.

When the Muslim army cannot bring back livestock from enemy territory, should they leave them for the enemy or destroy them? This passage from al-Hidayah presents the Hanafi view that slaughtering and burning is allowed, and responds to Imam al-Shafi'i's objection based on a hadith. The key is the concept of 'valid purpose' (gharad sahih) which overrides general prohibitions.

Guided Path
1
State the Scenario
Identify the situation: the imam is returning from enemy territory with livestock that cannot be transported to Dar al-Islam.
This is the trigger for the ruling.
2
Identify the Hanafi Ruling
According to the Hanafi school, the imam should slaughter the livestock and then burn them. He should not mutilate them nor leave them alive.
The ruling is based on istihsan for a valid purpose.
3
Identify the Shafi'i Position
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the livestock should be left alive, citing a hadith that prohibits slaughtering a sheep except for eating.
This is the opposing view.
4
Analyze the Shafi'i Dalil
The Shafi'i proof includes a hadith (though its authenticity is questioned) and the action of Abu Bakr advising not to kill animals except for food.
The Hanafi response addresses both points.
5
Analyze the Hanafi Response
The Hanafis argue that slaughtering for a valid purpose (weakening the enemy) is permissible, and the hadith either is weak or refers to burning alive, not slaughtering. Istihsan overrides the general prohibition when there is a greater benefit.
The response also distinguishes between slaughtering (permitted) and burning alive (prohibited).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا أَرَادَ الْإِمَامُ الْعَوْدَ وَمَعَةً مَوَاشٍ فَلَمْ يَقْدِرُ عَلَى نَفْلِهَا إِلَى دَارِ الْإِسْلَام ذَبَحَهَا وَحَرَّفَهَا وَلَا يَعْقِرُهَا وَلَايَتْرُكْهَا وقَالَ الشَّافِعِي يَتْرُكَهَا لِأَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ نَهى عَنْ ذَبْحِ الشَّاةِ إِلَّا لِمَا كَلَةٍ وَلَنَا اَنَّ ذَبُحَ الْحَيَوَانِ يَجُوزُ الغَرَضِ صَحِيح وَ لَا عَرَضَ اَصَحُ مِنْ كَسْرِ شَوْكَةِ الْأَعْدَاءِ ثُمَّ يُحْرَقُ بِالنَّارِ لِيَنْقَطِعَ مَنْفَعَتُهُ عَنِ الْكُفَّارِ وَصَارَ كَتَحْرِيب الْبُنْيَانِ بِخِلَافِ التَّحْرِيقِ قَبْلَ الذَّبْحِ لأَنه مَنهَى عَنْهُ وَبِخِلَافِ الْعَقْرِ لِأَنَّهُ مُثَلَةً وَتُحْرَقُ الْأَسْلِحَةُ أَيْضًا وَمَا لَا يَحْتَرِقُ مِنْهَا يُذقَنُ فِى مَوْضِعَ لَا يَطَّلِعُ عَلَيْهِ الْكُفَّارُ ابْطَالًا لِلْمَنْفَعَةِ عَلَيْهِمْ
ترجمہ اور جب امام دار الاسلام واپس آجانا چاہیں اور ان کے ساتھ مویشی ہوں جن کو اپنے ساتھ لانا ان کے بس کی بات نہ ہو تو ان کو ذبح کر کے آگ لگا دیں، ان کی قطع و برید نہ کریں اور نہ ہی زندہ چھوڑ کر چلے آئیں، اور امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ ان کو زندہ چھوڑ کر آجائیں، کیونکہ نبی کریم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے کھانے کے علاوہ کسی اور غرض سے بکر کی ذبح کرنے سے منع فرمایا ہے، ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ جانور کو کسی صحیح مقصد کیلئے ذبح کیا جا سکتا ہے، اور اس سے بڑھ کر کیا صحیح مقصد ہو سکتا ہے کہ دشمن کی شان وشوکت اور مالی حیثیت کمزور کرنے کیلئے ان کو ذبح کیا جائے ، اور پھر ان مویشیوں کو آگ لگادی جائے تا کہ وہ کفار کے کسی کام نہ آسکیں ، بالکل ویسا ہی جس طرح کہ عمارتوں کو برباد کر کے دشمن کو زک پہنچائی جاتی ہے۔ ہاں البتہ ذبح کرنے سے پہلے آگ لگانے کی اجازت نہیں ، اسی طرح قطع و برید بھی جائز نہیں ہے کہ اسے مثلہ کہا جاتا ہے، اسی طرح دشمن کے اسلحہ کو بھی آگ لگا دی جائے اور جو چیز آگ میں نہ جلتی ہو تو اسے ایسی جگہ دفن کر دیں جہاں دشمن کی پہنچ آسان نہ ہو ، تا کہ دشمن ان سے فائدہ نہ اٹھا سکے۔
تشریح متن ہدایہ کی مذکورہ عبارت کے مطابق کفر کی قوت کو توڑنے کیلئے ان تمام اسباب و لوازمات سے اس کو محروم رکھا جائے گا ۔۔ چنانچہ جہاد و قتال سے فراغت کے بعد دارالاسلام کی طرف واپس جاتے وقت جانوروں کو ذبح کر کے جلانا اسلحہ کو محفوظ مقام پر دفن کرنا ضروری امر ٹھہرا۔ بشرطیکہ ان ( جانوروں، اسلحہ وغیرہ) کی نقل مکانی ناممکن ہو۔ تا کہ کفر کی قوت وشوکت پارہ پارہ ہو جائے ۔ لیکن امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ جانوروں کو زندہ چھوڑ دے۔ کیونکہ رسول علیہ الصلوۃ والسلام نے کھانے کی ضرورت کے ماسواء بکری کو ذبح کرنے سے منع فرمایا ہے۔ لہذا کھانے کی غرض سے ذبح کرنا جائز ہے ورنہ نہیں لیکن بقول صاحب عین الہدایہ یہ حدیث کہیں منقول نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ حضرت ابوبکر صدیق نے شام کی طرف لشکر بھیجتے وقت یزید بن ابی سفیان کو دس باتوں کی وصیت کی تھی ان میں سے ایک وصیت جانوروں کو ذبح کرنے سے ممانعت سے متعلق بھی تھی ۔ یعنی کھانے کے علاوہ بکری یا گائے کو ہلاک نہ کریں۔ (رواه مالک ، ابن ابی شیبه ) امام شافعی کا استدلال اگر چه رسول علیہ الصلوۃ والسلام کی حدیث سے متحقق نہیں۔ لیکن حضرت ابو بکر صدیق کے خلیفہ راشد ہونے کے حوالے سے رسول علیہ الصلوۃ والسلام کی دوسری حدیث: عَلَيْكُمْ بِسُنَنِي وَسُنَّةِ الْخُلَفَاءِ الرَّاشِدِيْنَ تم پر میری اور خلفائے راشدین کی سنت لا زم ہے سے امام شافعی کا استدلال صحیح ثابت ہوتا ہے۔ مگر حضرت ابو بکر صدیق کی وصیت جانوروں کو زندہ جلانے کی صورت نہیں ہلاکت پر محمول ہوگی یا انہیں (جانوروں کو ) منتقل کرنے کی سہولت نہ ہونے پر بنی ہوگی۔ اگر جانوروں کی ہلاکت کے حوالے سے غرض صحیح موجود نہ ہوتو پھر امام شافعی کا قول معتبر متصور ہوگا۔ اگر غرض صحیح پائی جائے تو احناف کا موقف مبنی بر حق متصور ہوگا۔ اور جانوروں کو ذبح کر کے جلانے اور اسلحہ کو محفوظ مقام پر دفن کرنے سے کفر کی طاقت ختم ہوتی ہے تو اس سے بڑی غرض صحیح اور کیا ہو۔ پس ثابت ہوا کہ احناف کی رائے راج اور امام شافعی کا موقف مرجوح ہوگا۔
And when the imam intends to return, and with him are livestock, and he is not able to transport them to Dar al-Islam, he should slaughter them and burn them, and not mutilate them, and not leave them. And al-Shafi'i said: he should leave them, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) prohibited slaughtering a sheep except for eating. And our proof is that slaughtering an animal is permissible for a valid purpose, and no purpose is more valid than breaking the might of the enemies. Then he burns them with fire so that their benefit is cut off from the disbelievers, and it is like the demolition of buildings. Unlike burning before slaughter, because that is prohibited, and unlike mutilation (aqr), because that is mutilation (muthla). And weapons are also burned, and what does not burn from them is buried in a place where the disbelievers cannot access, to nullify their benefit. Translation: And when the imam wishes to return to Dar al-Islam, and he has livestock that he cannot transport, he should slaughter them and set them on fire, not mutilate them, nor leave them alive. Imam Shafi'i says he should leave them alive, because the Prophet (PBUH) prohibited slaughtering a goat except for eating. Our proof is that animals can be slaughtered for a valid purpose, and what greater valid purpose than weakening the enemy's prestige and wealth? Then they are set on fire so that they become useless to the disbelievers, just like demolishing buildings. However, setting fire before slaughtering is not allowed, nor is mutilation (aqr) as it is muthla. Similarly, the enemy's weapons should be burned, and what does not burn should be buried in a place inaccessible to the enemy, so that the enemy cannot benefit from them. Explanation: According to the above text of Hidayah, to break the power of disbelief, all means and equipment should be denied to them. So after finishing jihad and fighting, when returning to Dar al-Islam, it is necessary to slaughter and burn animals and to bury weapons in a safe place, provided transporting them is impossible. This is to shatter the power and might of disbelief. But Imam Shafi'i says to leave the animals alive, because the Prophet (PBUH) prohibited slaughtering a goat except for eating; thus slaughtering is allowed only for food. However, the author of 'Ain al-Hidayah says this hadith is not transmitted elsewhere. Rather, when Abu Bakr al-Siddiq sent an army to Syria, he advised Yazid ibn Abi Sufyan with ten things, one of which was prohibition of slaughtering animals except for eating (reported by Malik and Ibn Abi Shaybah). Imam Shafi'i's reasoning, though not established by a hadith of the Prophet, is supported by the hadith 'You must follow my Sunnah and the Sunnah of the Rightly Guided Caliphs.' However, Abu Bakr's advice is interpreted to apply to cases of burning alive, not to slaughtering for a valid purpose when transport is impossible. If there is no valid purpose for killing the animals, then Shafi'i's view is acceptable; but if there is a valid purpose (like weakening the enemy), then the Hanafi view is correct. Since slaughtering and burning animals and burying weapons destroys the power of disbelief, there can be no greater valid purpose. Thus, the Hanafi opinion is preponderant and Shafi'i's is outweighed.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage deals with the situation when the Muslim army is returning from enemy territory and has livestock that cannot be transported. The Hanafi position, supported by istihsan, allows slaughtering and burning the animals to prevent them from falling into enemy hands, as this weakens their military and economic strength. Imam al-Shafi'i disallows this, citing a hadith prohibiting slaughter except for eating. The Hanafi response: the hadith may not be authentic (as per 'Ain al-Hidayah) or is specific to normal circumstances; in jihad, a valid purpose overrides the general prohibition. The commentary further refines by distinguishing between slaughtering (permitted) and burning alive (prohibited). The Hanafi view is considered preponderant (rajih) when there is a clear military benefit.

Key Terms
الذبح (al-dhabh): Religious slaughter of animals; in this context, slaughtering livestock to prevent enemy benefit.
التحريق (al-tahriq): Burning after slaughter; permitted to destroy benefit for the enemy.
المثلة (al-muthla): Mutilation of a dead body; prohibited in Islam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what should the imam do with livestock that cannot be transported when returning from enemy territory?
A) Leave them alive and return.
B) Mutilate them and leave.
C) Slaughter them and burn them.
D) Burn them alive.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the imam may slaughter and burn livestock when transport is impossible to deprive the enemy, based on the principle of istihsan for a valid purpose.

Dividing Spoils in Enemy Territory: Hanafi Positions
Intra-Hanafi dispute on dividing spoils in enemy territory

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi positions on dividing spoils in Dar al-Harb and apply the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
Division of spoils in Dar al-Harb is invalid according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf; Muhammad considers it merely disliked.

The division of war spoils (ghanimah) is a critical issue in Islamic law of jihad. A key dispute within the Hanafi school concerns whether such division can take place while the army is still in enemy territory (Dar al-Harb). This lesson unpacks the arguments, the underlying principle of ihraz (secure possession), and the final relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
State the issue and three positions
Identify that the dispute is about dividing spoils in Dar al-Harb. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say it is not valid (la yajuz), Muhammad says it is disliked (makruh tanzih), and al-Shafi'i says it is permissible.
The intra-Hanafi dispute is between Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.
2
Identify the usul principle
The core difference is when ownership of spoils is established. Hanafi: ownership requires secure possession (ihraz) in Dar al-Islam. Shafi'i: mere possession (istila') in Dar al-Harb suffices.
This principle affects several related issues.
3
Evaluate the Hanafi dalil
The Prophet prohibited selling spoils in Dar al-Harb. Division (qismah) is a notional sale (bay' ma'ni), so it falls under the prohibition. This is a dalil naqli (hadith).
The hadith is ahad, but accepted in Hanafi usul.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Muhammad al-Shaybani interprets the prohibition as indicating karahah tanzih (dislike) rather than absolute prohibition (tahrim). He holds that division is not sinful but it is better to delay until Dar al-Islam.
The difference hinges on the weight given to the hadith.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position for fatwa is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: division in Dar al-Harb is not valid and does not transfer ownership. This is the safer opinion.
Later Hanafi jurists have preferred this view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يُقَسَّمُ عَيْمَةً فِي دَارِ الْحَرْبِ حَتَّى يَخْرُجَها إلى دار الإسلام وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِي لَا بَأْسَ بِذَالِكَ وَأَصْلُهُ أَنَّ الْمُلْكَ لِلْعَادِمِينَ لَا يَثْبُتُ قَبْلَ الْإِحْرَازِ بِدَارِ الْإِسْلَامِ عِندَنَا وَعِندَهُ يَثْبُتُ وَيُستَنِي عَلَى هَذَا الْأَصْلِ عِدَّةُ مِّنَ الْمَسَائِلِ ذَكَرُنَا هَافِى كِفَايَةِ الْمُنتَهى لَهُ أَنَّ سَبَبَ الْمِلْكِ الْإِسْتِيْلَاءُ إِذَا وَرَدَ عَلَى مَالِ مُبَاحِ كَمَا فِي الصُّوْدِ وَلَا مَعْنى لِلِاسْتِيلاء سِوَى إِثْبَاتِ الْيَدِ وَقَدْ تَحَقَّقَ وَلَنَا أَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ نَهَى عَنْ بَيْعِ الْغَنِيمَةِ فِي دَارِ الْحَرْبِ وَالْخِلَاف ثَابِتُ فِيهِ وَالْقِسْمَةُ بَيْعٌ مَعْنِي فَتَدْخُلُ تَحَتَهُ وَلِأَنَّ الإِسْتِيلَاءَ إِثْبَاتُ الْبَدِ الْحَافِظَةِ وَالسَّاقِلَةِ وَالثَّانِي مُنْعَدِمُ لِقُدْرَتِهِمْ عَلَى الْإِسْتِفَادِ وَفَجُوْدُهُ ظَاهِرُ ثُمَّ قِيلَ مَوْضِعُ الخِلافِ تَرَتُبُ الْأَحْكَامِ عَلَى الْقِسْمَةِ إِذَا قَسَمَ الْإِمَامُ لَا عَنِ اجْتِهَا دِ لأَنَّ حُكْمَ الْمِلْكِ لَا يَثْبُتُ بِدُونِهِ وَقِيلَ الْكَرَاهَةُ وَهِيَ كَرَاهَةٌ تَنْزِيهِ عِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ فَإِنَّهُ قَالَ عَلَى قَوْلِ ابِي حَنِيفَةَ وَ أبِى يُوسُفَ لَا يَجُوزُ الْقِسْمَةُ فِي دَارِ الْحَرْبِ وَعِندَ مُحَمَّدٍ الْأَفْضَلُ أَنْ يُقَسمَ فِى دَارِ الْإِسْلَامِ وَوَجْهُ الْكَرَاهَةِ أَنَّ دَلِيلَ الْمُطْلَانِ رَاجِعُ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ تَقَاعَدَ عَنْ سَبَبٍ
And spoils are not divided in Dar al-Harb until they are taken out to Dar al-Islam. And al-Shafi'i said: there is nothing wrong with that. And its underlying principle is that ownership for the gainers is not established before secure possession (ihraz) in Dar al-Islam according to us, whereas according to him it is established. And on this principle depend several issues which we have mentioned in Kifayat al-Muntaha. For him, the cause of ownership is istila' (possession) when it occurs on permitted property, like in hunting, and there is no meaning of istila' except establishing physical control (yad), and that has been actualized. And for us, the Prophet (peace be upon him) prohibited the sale of spoils in Dar al-Harb, and the disagreement about it is established, and division is a notional sale, so it falls under that. And because istila' is the establishment of the protecting hand and the transporting hand, and the latter is absent due to their ability to recover possession? And its presence is apparent. Then it is said: the point of disagreement is the attachment of rulings to division when the imam divides without ijtihad? Because ownership does not become established without it. And it is said: it is disliked (karahah), and it is a tanzihi dislike according to Muhammad, for he said: according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, division is not permissible in Dar al-Harb, but according to Muhammad, it is better to divide in Dar al-Islam. And the basis of the dislike is that the evidence of the two is returnable? except that it falls short of a cause.
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the division of spoils (ghanimah) while still in Dar al-Harb. The underlying usul principle: according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, ownership of spoils for the soldiers is not established until the spoils are brought to Dar al-Islam (ihraz). Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees and considers ownership established by mere possession in enemy territory. The Hanafi proof includes the Prophet's prohibition of selling spoils in Dar al-Harb; since division (qismah) is akin to a sale, it is also prohibited. Additionally, istila' (possession) requires both physical control and the ability to transport securely, which is lacking in enemy territory. Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani differs: he considers division permissible but makruh tanzih (disliked), and it is better to divide in Dar al-Islam. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) for fatwa is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: division in Dar al-Harb is not valid.

Key Terms
الغنيمة (al-ghanimah): Spoils of war taken from the enemy after battle; includes movable property.
الإحراز (al-ihraz): Secure possession and transport of spoils into Dar al-Islam, necessary for ownership.
الاستيلاء (al-istila'): Physical control over property; in Hanafi fiqh, it requires both a protecting hand and a transporting hand.
البيع المعنى (al-bay' al-ma'ni): Notional sale; a transaction that has the legal effect of a sale (like division) even if not a formal sale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what is the ruling on dividing spoils in Dar al-Harb?
A) Permissible and recommended.
B) Not permissible (la yajuz) and ownership not established.
C) Permissible but disliked (makruh tanzih).
D) Permissible only if the imam divides by ijtihad.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is that division of spoils in Dar al-Harb is not valid; ownership requires secure possession (ihraz) in Dar al-Islam.

Hanafi vs Shafi'i: Destroying Enemy Property After Jihad
Hanafi vs Shafi'i dispute on destroying animals/weapons after war

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on destroying enemy property after jihad, explain the Shafi'i counterargument, and identify which view is preponderant (mufta bihi).

Core Idea
If transporting enemy property is impossible, destroying it to weaken kufr is necessary (wajib) in the Hanafi school.

When Muslim fighters conquer enemy territory but cannot bring captured animals and weapons back to Dar al-Islam, what should they do? The Hanafi school rules that destroying such property is necessary to prevent the enemy from regaining strength. But Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, citing a prophetic prohibition and the instruction of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq. This lesson unpacks the proofs and determines which view is relied upon.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling: after jihad, when transport is impossible, it is necessary (ضروری) to slaughter/burn animals and bury weapons to break the power of kufr.
Note the condition: transport impossibility (عدم امکان نقل مکانی).
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that animals should be left alive, based on a reported hadith prohibiting killing livestock except for food, and on Abu Bakr's advice to Yazid ibn Abi Sufyan.
The hadith is questioned for authenticity in the Hanafi commentary.
3
Examine the proofs of both sides
Hanafi proof: general principle of depriving kufr of strength, and absence of authentic prohibition. Shafi'i proof: a prophetic hadith (according to him) and the practice of Abu Bakr supported by the hadith 'Follow my Sunnah and the Sunnah of the rightly-guided caliphs.'
The Hanafi commentary argues the prophetic hadith is not established.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i dalil
The Hanafi response: the prophetic hadith is unverified; Abu Bakr's instruction was not about burning alive but about killing, and it was given when transport was possible. When transport is impossible and a valid purpose (غرض صحیح) exists, slaughtering is allowed.
The condition of valid purpose (weakening kufr) is decisive.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and tarjih
Practical difference: Hanafis destroy such property; Shafi'is leave it if transport possible, and if not, they also permit killing for a valid purpose but with reluctance. The Hanafi view is preponderant (راجح) because of the clear valid purpose of weakening kufr.
In case no valid purpose exists, the Shafi'i view is followed per the commentary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تشریح متن ہدایہ کی مذکورہ عبارت کے مطابق کفر کی قوت کو توڑنے کیلئے ان تمام اسباب و لوازمات سے اس کو محروم رکھا جائے گا ۔۔ چنانچہ جہاد و قتال سے فراغت کے بعد دارالاسلام کی طرف واپس جاتے وقت جانوروں کو ذبح کر کے جلانا اسلحہ کو محفوظ مقام پر دفن کرنا ضروری امر ٹھہرا۔ بشرطیکہ ان ( جانوروں، اسلحہ وغیرہ) کی نقل مکانی ناممکن ہو۔ تا کہ کفر کی قوت وشوکت پارہ پارہ ہو جائے ۔ لیکن امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ جانوروں کو زندہ چھوڑ دے۔ کیونکہ رسول علیہ الصلوۃ والسلام نے کھانے کی ضرورت کے ماسواء بکری کو ذبح کرنے سے منع فرمایا ہے۔ لہذا کھانے کی غرض سے ذبح کرنا جائز ہے ورنہ نہیں لیکن بقول صاحب عین الہدایہ یہ حدیث کہیں منقول نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ حضرت ابوبکر صدیق نے شام کی طرف لشکر بھیجتے وقت یزید بن ابی سفیان کو دس باتوں کی وصیت کی تھی ان میں سے ایک وصیت جانوروں کو ذبح کرنے سے ممانعت سے متعلق بھی تھی ۔ یعنی کھانے کے علاوہ بکری یا گائے کو ہلاک نہ کریں۔ (رواه مالک ، ابن ابی شیبه ) امام شافعی کا استدلال اگر چه رسول علیہ الصلوۃ والسلام کی حدیث سے متحقق نہیں۔ لیکن حضرت ابو بکر صدیق کے خلیفہ راشد ہونے کے حوالے سے رسول علیہ الصلوۃ والسلام کی دوسری حدیث
عَلَيْكُمْ بِسُنَنِي وَسُنَّةِ الْخُلَفَاءِ الرَّاشِدِيْنَ
تم پر میری اور خلفائے راشدین کی سنت لا زم ہے
سے امام شافعی کا استدلال صحیح ثابت ہوتا ہے۔ مگر حضرت ابو بکر صدیق کی وصیت جانوروں کو زندہ جلانے کی صورت نہیں ہلاکت پر محمول ہوگی یا انہیں (جانوروں کو ) منتقل کرنے کی سہولت نہ ہونے پر بنی ہوگی۔ اگر جانوروں کی ہلاکت کے حوالے سے غرض صحیح موجود نہ ہوتو پھر امام شافعی کا قول معتبر متصور ہوگا۔ اگر غرض صحیح پائی جائے تو احناف کا موقف مبنی بر حق متصور ہوگا۔ اور جانوروں کو ذبح کر کے جلانے اور اسلحہ کو محفوظ مقام پر دفن کرنے سے کفر کی طاقت ختم ہوتی ہے تو اس سے بڑی غرض صحیح اور کیا ہو۔ پس ثابت ہوا کہ احناف کی رائے راج اور امام شافعی کا موقف مرجوح ہوگا۔
Commentary on the above text of Hidayah: According to it, to break the power of kufr, all those means and necessities will be denied to it. Thus, after completing jihad and fighting, when returning to Dar al-Islam, it is necessary to slaughter and burn animals and bury weapons in a safe place, provided that their transport is impossible. So that the power and might of kufr becomes shattered. But Imam Shafi'i says: leave the animals alive, because the Messenger (peace be upon him) forbade slaughtering goats except for the need of food. Therefore, slaughtering for food is permissible, otherwise not. But according to the author of 'Ayn al-Hidayah, this hadith is not narrated anywhere. Rather, when Sayyiduna Abu Bakr al-Siddiq sent an army towards Syria, he gave ten instructions to Yazid ibn Abi Sufyan, among which one instruction was about the prohibition of slaughtering animals, i.e., do not kill goats or cows except for food. (Narrated by Malik, Ibn Abi Shaybah). Although Imam Shafi'i's inference from the hadith of the Messenger (peace be upon him) is not verified, but through the hadith of the Messenger (peace be upon him) regarding Sayyiduna Abu Bakr al-Siddiq being a righteous caliph: 'You must follow my Sunnah and the Sunnah of the rightly-guided caliphs,' Imam Shafi'i's inference becomes correct. However, the instruction of Sayyiduna Abu Bakr al-Siddiq is not about burning animals alive; it will be interpreted as killing, or it was based on the lack of facility to transport them. If there is no valid purpose regarding the killing of animals, then Imam Shafi'i's view will be considered reliable. If a valid purpose is found, then the Hanafi stance will be considered correct. And what greater valid purpose is there than destroying the power of kufr by slaughtering and burning animals and burying weapons in a safe place? Thus it is proven that the Hanafi view is preponderant and Imam Shafi'i's position is weaker.
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the destruction of enemy property after jihad. The Hanafi position, based on the above text of Hidayah, holds that if animals, weapons, etc., cannot be transported back to Dar al-Islam, they must be slaughtered, burned, or buried to prevent the enemy from using them and to break their power. This is considered necessary (ضروری). Imam Shafi'i argues that animals should be left alive, relying on a prophetic prohibition against killing livestock except for food, and on the instruction of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq. The Hanafi commentary rebuts that the prophetic hadith is not authentically known, and Abu Bakr's instruction was not about burning alive but about killing, and only when transport is difficult. The commentary concludes that if there is a valid purpose (such as weakening the enemy), the Hanafi view prevails; otherwise, Shafi'i's view is followed. The Hanafi position is considered preponderant here.

Key Terms
محروم رکھنا (mahrūm rakhnā): To deprive the enemy of means of strength such as animals and weapons.
غرض صحیح (gharad ṣaḥīḥ): A valid, legitimate purpose recognized by Shari'ah, such as weakening the enemy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi commentary, when is it permissible to slaughter animals after jihad?
A) Always, as a routine practice
B) Only for food
C) When transport to Dar al-Islam is impossible and there is a valid purpose like weakening the enemy
D) Never; Shafi'i's position is always followed

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, destroying enemy property after jihad is wajib only when transport is impossible and there is a valid purpose (weakening kufr); otherwise, the Shafi'i view of preservation is followed.

Division of Spoils in Dar al-Harb vs Dar al-Islam
Hanafi ruling and proof that spoils cannot be divided in Dar al-Harb until brought to Dar al-Islam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on dividing spoils in Dar al-Harb, explain the Hanafi proof based on incomplete istila, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Ownership of spoils completes only after ihraz in Dar al-Islam; until then, division is invalid.

This lesson examines a key dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the timing of dividing spoils of war. At issue is whether ownership is established immediately upon capture (istila) or only after the spoils are secured in Dar al-Islam. We will trace the Hanafi proof from the Prophetic prohibition of selling spoils in enemy territory, analyze the definition of istila, and see how this principle yields different rulings in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested ruling
The passage explicitly contrasts the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on dividing spoils in Dar al-Harb. Note that the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is that it is not permissible (la yajuz), while Imam Muhammad considers it only makruh tanzihi.
2
Analyze the underlying principle: ownership and ihraz
The Hanafi argument hinges on the concept that ownership does not vest until the spoils are secured (ihraz) in Dar al-Islam. Contrast this with the Shafi'i view that istila (taking control) alone suffices, analogous to hunting.
Hanafis require both yad hafizah (protective hand) and yad salikah (controlling/transporting hand).
3
Examine the Hanafi proof (dalil)
The text alludes to the Prophetic prohibition of selling spoils in Dar al-Harb. Qiyas extends this to division, as both involve transfer of ownership before full control. Identify the illa: incomplete control due to the enemy's ability to recapture.
The dalil is a hadith (dalil naqli) and qiyas.
4
Understand the Shafi'i counter-argument
Al-Shafi'i argues that istila alone establishes ownership, citing the example of hunting where mere capture confers ownership. The Hanafi response distinguishes between permissible property (hunting) and enemy property (which requires additional security).
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If division occurs in Dar al-Harb, for Hanafis it is invalid (unless Muhammad's view is followed, where it is valid but disliked). For Shafi'is, it is valid. This affects inheritance, sale, and other legal effects of ownership.
The mufta bihi (operative position) is the prohibition of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يُقَسَّمُ الْغَنِيمَةَ فِي دَارِ الْحَرْبِ حَتَّى يَخْرُجَ بِهَا إِلَى دَارِ الْإِسْلَامِ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِي لَا بَأْسَ بِذَلِكَ وَأَصْلُهُ أَنَّ الْمِلْكَ لِلْغَانِمِينَ لَا يَثْبُتُ قَبْلَ الْإِحْرَازِ بِدَارِ الْإِسْلَامِ عِنْدَنَا وَعِنْدَهُ يَثْبُتُ وَيَتَرَتَّبُ عَلَى هَذَا الْأَصْلِ عِدَّةُ مَسَائِلَ ذَكَرْنَا هَا هُنَا فِي كِفَايَةِ الْمُنْتَهَى لَهُ أَنَّ سَبَبَ الْمِلْكِ الْاسْتِيلَاءُ إِذَا وَرَدَ عَلَى مَالٍ مُبَاحٍ كَمَا فِي الصَّيْدِ وَلَا مَعْنَى لِلِاسْتِيلَاءِ سِوَى إِثْبَاتِ الْيَدِ الْحَافِظَةِ وَالسَّالِكَةِ وَالثَّانِي مُنْعَدِمٌ لِقُدْرَتِهِمْ عَلَى الِاسْتِفَادَةِ وَوُجُودُهُ ظَاهِرٌ ثُمَّ قِيلَ مَوْضِعُ الْخِلَافِ تَرْتِيبُ الْأَحْكَامِ عَلَى الْقِسْمَةِ إِذَا قَسَمَ الْإِمَامُ لَا عَنِ اجْتِهَادٍ لِأَنَّ حُكْمَ الْمِلْكِ لَا يَثْبُتُ بِدُونِهِ وَقِيلَ الْكَرَاهَةُ وَهِيَ كَرَاهَةٌ تَنْزِيهِيَّةٌ عِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ فَإِنَّهُ قَالَ عَلَى قَوْلِ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَأَبِي يُوسُفَ لَا يَجُوزُ الْقِسْمَةُ فِي دَارِ الْحَرْبِ وَعِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ الْأَفْضَلُ أَنْ يُقْسَمَ فِي دَارِ الْإِسْلَامِ وَوَجْهُ الْكَرَاهَةِ أَنَّ دَلِيلَ الْإِطْلَاقِ رَاجِعٌ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ تَقَاعَدَ عَنْ سَبَبِ الْجَوَازِ فَلَا يَتَقَاعَدُ عَنْ إِثْبَاتِ الْكَرَاهَةِ
And the imam shall not divide the spoils in Dar al-Harb until he brings them out to Dar al-Islam. Al-Shafi'i said: There is no harm in that. The basis of this is that ownership for the fighters is not established before securing in Dar al-Islam according to us, but according to him it is established. Several sub-issues arise from this principle, which we have mentioned here in Kifayat al-Muntaha. For him, the cause of ownership is istila (taking control) when it falls on permissible property, as in hunting. And istila has no meaning other than establishing the protective and controlling hand. The second (controlling hand) is absent due to their ability to recover it, and its existence is apparent. Then it is said: the point of dispute is the effect of the division when the imam divides without ijtihad, because the ruling of ownership is not established without it. And it is said: (the dispute) is about karahah (dislike), and it is karahah tanzihiyyah according to Muhammad, for he said: According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, division in Dar al-Harb is not permissible, and according to Muhammad it is better to divide in Dar al-Islam. The basis of karahah is that the evidence of permissibility returns, but it falls short of the cause of permissibility, so it does not fall short of establishing karahah.
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute about when spoils of war can be divided. The Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf) is that the imam must not divide the spoils in Dar al-Harb; they must first be brought to Dar al-Islam. Imam Shafi'i allows division in Dar al-Harb. The underlying principle is whether ownership of the spoils is established before they are secured in Dar al-Islam. Hanafis say no, because true control (istila) requires both taking possession and the ability to protect and transport the goods; in Dar al-Harb, the enemy can still retake them, so the second condition is missing. Shafi'i analogizes to hunting, where mere capture establishes ownership. The Hanafi response includes a proof that the Prophet forbade selling spoils in Dar al-Harb, and division is like a sale. The passage also clarifies an intra-Hanafi nuance: Imam Muhammad considers it only makruh tanzihi (disliked, not prohibited) to divide in Dar al-Harb, while Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say it is not permissible (la yajuz). Thus the operative ruling is prohibition. The sub-issues (not fully detailed here) include that a fighter who has intercourse with a slave-girl in Dar al-Harb does not establish paternity or umm walad status, etc.

Key Terms
الاستيلاء (al-istīlā’): Taking physical control and possession of property, which is the cause of ownership according to Shafi'i; for Hanafis it requires both taking and securing.
الإحراز (al-iḥrāz): Securing the spoils in a safe place (Dar al-Islam) such that the enemy cannot easily recapture them.
كراهة تنزيهية (karāhah tanzīhiyyah): A light dislike (makruh tanzihi) as per Imam Muhammad, meaning it is better to avoid but not sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), what is the ruling on dividing spoils in Dar al-Harb?
A) It is permissible (ja'iz)
B) It is not permissible (la yajuz)
C) It is recommended (mustahabb)
D) It is only disliked (makruh tanzihi)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires spoils to be secured in Dar al-Islam before division, because true ownership only vests when the enemy cannot easily recapture the goods.

Ruling on Dividing Spoils in Dar al-Harb
Intra-Hanafi dispute on dividing ghanimah in enemy territory

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi positions on dividing ghanimah in Dar al-Harb and explain the basis for the difference.

Core Idea
Dividing spoils in enemy territory is makruh tanzih according to Imam Muhammad, but impermissible according to the elder two.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi disagreement on a practical question of jihad: when may war booty be divided? The core issue is whether the risk of invalidation in Dar al-Harb renders the division impermissible or merely disliked. Understanding this dispute sharpens your grasp of how the Hanafi masters balanced textual proofs and practical considerations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the disputed ruling
The act is dividing ghanimah while still in enemy territory (Dar al-Harb). The dispute is about its legal status: permissible with dislike, or outright impermissible.
2
Differentiate the two Hanafi positions
Imam Muhammad holds it is makruh tanzih (permissible but better avoided). Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold it is not permissible (ghayr ja'iz, which in this context implies haram).
3
Analyse the reasoning behind the difference
Imam Muhammad acknowledges that the division could be invalidated (batil) if conditions are not met, but considers this risk insufficient to render the act haram; hence only karahah tanzihiyyah. The two elders give more weight to the risk and consider the act impermissible.
Note that the word 'ja'iz' in the text translates as 'permissible'; its negation here implies prohibition, not mere invalidity.
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The difference is whether the division is valid if performed in Dar al-Harb. If it is makruh tanzih, the division is valid but disliked; if impermissible, the division is invalid and must be re-done in Dar al-Islam.
5
Assess the mufta bihi
The text does not specify which view is relied upon for fatwa. Later Hanafi works often give precedence to Imam Muhammad's view in matters of mu'amalat when no strong contrary evidence exists, but students should consult a reliable fatwa collection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب السير اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ہفتم ہے۔ چنانچہ امام محمد کے نزدیک اس میں کراہت تنزیہی ہے۔ چنانچہ امام محمد نے سیر کبیر میں کہا ہے کہ امام ابو حنیفہ اور ابو یوسفہ کے قول کے مطابق دارالحرب میں مال غنیمت کی تقسیم جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور امام محمد کے نزدیک افضل یہ ہے کہ دارالاسلام میں واپس آ کر تقسیم کرے۔ اس کراہت کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ وہاں رہتے ہوئے تقسیم کا باطل ہونا ہی راجح قول ہے۔ مگر یہ دلیل جائز نہ ہونے پر موثر نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ سے کم کراہت تو ضرور پیدا ہوگی۔
Chapter of Siyar. This is Ashraf al-Bidayah, Urdu commentary on Hidayah, Volume 7. So according to Imam Muhammad, there is karahah tanzihiyyah in it. So Imam Muhammad said in Siyar al-Kabir that according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, dividing the spoils in Dar al-Harb is not permissible. And according to Imam Muhammad, it is better to return to Dar al-Islam and divide there. The reason for this karahah is that the nullification of division while staying there is the preponderant view. But this proof is not effective on impermissibility, because at least karahah tanzihiyyah would occur.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the ruling of dividing war booty (ghanimah) while still in enemy territory (Dar al-Harb). The base text (probably from al-Hidayah) states a ruling, and the commentator explains the differences. According to Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, the permissible view allows division in Dar al-Harb with karahah tanzihiyyah (slight dislike). The same view is recorded in his Siyar al-Kabir. However, Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf hold that such division is not permissible (meaning it is prohibited). Imam Muhammad acknowledges their view but considers it better to postpone division until returning to Dar al-Islam. The reason for karahah is the possibility that the division could be invalidated (batil) if some condition is not met, but this possibility is not strong enough to render the act fully impermissible; hence only tanzih dislike attaches.

Key Terms
کراہت تنزیہی (karahah tanzihiyyah): A degree of dislike close to lawful (halal), but better to avoid; not sinful.
دار الحرب (Dar al-Harb): Territory under non-Muslim control where the rulings of war apply.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Makruh tanzih, and it is better to divide after returning to Dar al-Islam
C) Permissible without any dislike
D) Mustahabb (recommended)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school contains an internal disagreement on dividing spoils in Dar al-Harb: Imam Muhammad allows it with slight dislike, while the Sahibayn prohibit it, illustrating how risk assessment can lead to different rulings within the same methodological framework.
